Summer 1628 — Sixty Sail Against the Seawall

June – August 1628 · resolved at the table 5 February 2022 (deployment fixed 15 December 2021) · Mission: Siege · Theater: the seawall of La Rochelle

The situation

The summer’s shape was set months in advance. On 15 December the Narrator announced, “The Minister of War decides the composition of forces for the summer campaign,” and rolled:

🎲 The Minister of War rolls 1d6 — 4; 1d6 — 1

Narrator — “A single field army will be deployed, with every brigade except the Horse Guards and the 1st Brigade of Foot.”

Narrator — “This will be a Siege campaign.”

On 5 February the books opened on the season itself:

Narrator — “The Summer Campaign”

Narrator — “The siege of La Rochelle continues. The English navy, under the Admiral of the Fleet, the Earl of Lindsey, has assembled a flotilla of 29 warships and 31 merchantmen, ready to force their way past the sea wall and either break the siege, or evacuate the city entirely.”

Narrator — “It is the largest naval assault ever conducted against the French homeland. If the English are able to breach the seawall, a fortification devised by Cardinal Richelieu himself, they will have direct access to the city, and the rebellion will spread like a cancer. This is the last chance to contain the Protestant venom.”

Narrator — “The Cardinal himself has taken to the field, and will command the army on this campaign. He has positioned his headquarters on the seawall itself, and has consecrated every stone as a fortress in defense of God and France.”

The order of battle

Narrator — “The Field Army consists of the following:

1st Division: Lt. Gen. Bernard Lefebvre Guards Brigade: Bg. Gen. Alphonse Joseph Leclerc - Royal Foot Guards: Lt. Col. @Jules Lavelle - Cardinal’s Guard - King’s Musketeers: Lt. Col. Adhemar Lucy - - F Company enlisted: Sub. @Slade Imbee RNH

2nd Division: Lt. Gen. Frank Bouchard 2nd Brigade of Foot: Bg. Gen. Xavier Cherbuliez - 13th Fusiliers - 53rd Fusiliers 3rd Brigade of Foot - 27th Musketeers - 4th Arquebusiers 4th Brigade of Foot - 69th Arqubusiers - Gascon Regiment

Frontier Division

Cavalry Division: Lt. Gen. Denis Nee Heavy Brigade: Bg. Gen. Jean-Martin Desjardins - Crown Prince Cuirassiers: Col. Gaël Roquebert - - 1st Squadron: Lt. Col. @ArcticFox - Archduke Leopold Cuirassiers Dragoon Brigade”

The player characters in the line of battle:

Character Rank / Post Station
Jules Lavelle Baron, Lieutenant Colonel Royal Foot Guards, Guards Brigade, 1st Division
Slade Imbee Subaltern F Company, King’s Musketeers, Guards Brigade — the “newest subaltern in the King’s Musketeers,” promoted after the spring’s beach fighting
Jean Renault Lieutenant Colonel 1st Squadron, Crown Prince Cuirassiers, Heavy Brigade, Cavalry Division

The NPC command, as the record would soon characterize them: Cardinal Richelieu, in supreme command from his headquarters on the wall — “For all his fervor, the Cardinal has little military background.” Lt. Gen. Bernard Lefebvre, who “believes he understands the English mind well.” Bg. Gen. Alphonse Joseph Leclerc, whose adjutant would shortly stare “like Leclerc has gone mad.” Lt. Gen. Denis Nee, ordered to ‘use his discretion.’ And Bg. Gen. Jean-Martin Desjardins, dim rememberer of old military texts.

The Cardinal addressed his officers before the fleet came on:

Narrator — “The Cardinal addresses his officers. ‘So long as the Huguenots have a foothold in France, the King will never be master within his own borders or be able to enter upon any glorious undertaking without. It is incumbent upon us this day, with the English fleet bearing down on our defenses with the full fury of the Adversary on their side, that we put down this menace to Christian, and preserve the security of France, her people, and her God forevermore. Amen!’”

The record

Supreme command — Cardinal Richelieu

Narrator — “The Cardinal delivers his orders, arranging the army in a horseshoe pattern to catch any stray English in their net.”

🎲 The Cardinal’s command roll: 1d6 — 1

Narrator — “For all his fervor, the Cardinal has little military background. The English admiral, noting the broad array facing his forces, opts to concentrate his push on one section of the seawall, wreaking tremendous damage. The result is 5 - Broken by sortie.”

1st Division — Lt. Gen. Bernard Lefebvre

Narrator — “Lt. Gen. Lefebvre believes he understands the English mind well. He instructs his elite units to put their sharpshooting to the test, to try to pick off English officers aboard the attacking ships.”

🎲 Lt. Gen. Lefebvre’s command roll: 1d6 — 2

Narrator — “His plan fails; skilled as the men are, the rolling waves, and huddled-together English soldiery, makes it nearly impossible to distinguish common man from officer. Still, the bullets do find home in English flesh. The result is 4 - Inconclusive.”

Guards Brigade — Bg. Gen. Alphonse Joseph Leclerc

Narrator — “Bg. Gen. Leclerc, realizing the full might of the English command staff will remain to direct the attack, orders his section of the seawall abandoned. His adjutant stares like Leclerc has gone mad, but he hushes the young officer and continues with the orderly evacuation.”

🎲 Bg. Gen. Leclerc’s command roll: 1d6 — 4

Narrator — “As the English ships collide with the empty section of the seawall, disgorging their howling passengers, the planned charge across the fortification is halted by the realization that the mortar for this part of the seawall has yet to fully settle! The English charge back onto their boats before the weight of the landing causes them to settle entirely. The attack is partly slowed, but not stopped. The result is 3 - Inconclusive.”

The Royal Foot Guards — Lt. Col. Jules Lavelle

Narrator — “Lt. Col. @Jules Lavelle, give your orders.”

Jules Lavelle — “Appalled at the evident cowardice displayed by his commander, Jules orders his men to charge after the English, hoping to board and seize one of the merchantmen. ‘For the Glory of Lavelle!’”

Lavelle’s command dice had come up six two campaigns running — a six in the Norman bocage in winter, a six on the beaches in spring. The streak chose this moment, at the rail of an English warship, to end.

🎲 Lt. Col. Lavelle’s command roll: 1d6 — 1

Narrator — “Jules manages to lead his men up onto the deck of a warship instead, where they are met by the astonishment, and professional savagery, of seasoned English sea dogs. The Royal Foot Guards are butchered, sent into the sea by flight or in pieces. The result is 6 - Scattered by sortie.”

A single musket emoji rose over the message in salute.

The King’s Musketeers — Lt. Col. Adhemar Lucy

Narrator — “Lt. Col. Adhemar Lucy directs the King’s Musketeers to follow the general’s orders, maintaining the sniper fire even under retreat.”

🎲 Lt. Col. Lucy’s command roll: 1d6 — 5

Narrator — “The shots are no more damaging than before, though no great harm befalls his men. The result is 3 - Inconclusive.”

The Cavalry Division — Lt. Gen. Denis Nee

Narrator — “As the 2nd Division maintains the rest of the seawall, the Cavalry Division finds itself milling about on land. Lt. Gen. Denis Nee has been ordered to ‘use his discretion’ in choosing where and how to meet the enemy. With little idea how the English might attack, he has chosen to arrange the Heavy Brigade on the northern shore, and the Dragoons Brigade on the southern. If the English attempt a landing, his men will be ready.”

🎲 Lt. Gen. Nee’s command roll: 1d6 — 2

Narrator — “Unfortunately, while his men are ready, Nee is not – he is still arranging the Dragoons to the south when half of the English fleet redirects its efforts from the failing seawall to make a landing on the northern shore. The result is 5 - Broken by sortie.”

The Heavy Brigade — Bg. Gen. Jean-Martin Desjardins

Narrator — “As the English disembark, Bg. Gen. Desjardins frantically considers how he can possibly repel an infantry charge with a couple regiments of horse. He dimly recalls an old military text that recommended something called gorilla tactics. He doesn’t know quite what it means, but orders his men to ride into the woods, which he imagines is where a gorilla would prefer to fight.”

🎲 Bg. Gen. Desjardins’s command roll: 1d6 — 4

Narrator — “Over half the English follow the Heavy Brigade away from the shore, their strategic concerns overtaken by bloodlust. Unable to catch up with the horse, they accomplish little. It is not a glorious victory, but it is a real one for the Heavy Brigade. The result is 3 - Inconclusive.”

1st Squadron, Crown Prince Cuirassiers — Lt. Col. Jean Renault

Narrator — “@ArcticFox, give your orders and roll.”

Jean Renault — “we will flank the English as they chase Desjardins”

Jean Renault — “Avoiding the charge we ride to battle men!”

🎲 Lt. Col. Renault’s command roll: 1d6 — 6

Narrator — “The Crown Prince Cuirassiers attempt to break away from the rest of the brigade and circle back to find the English, but before they can form lines and return to give battle, the English have already given up and returned to their boats. The result is 3 - Inconclusive.”

The close of the battle

Narrator — “The rest of the battle proceeds similarly – having gotten the lay of the land, the English then pull back without taking serious losses. The siege continues, but the core of the English fleet remains a threat, and retreats to the open sea to regroup. The Cardinal declares the day an enormous success. As the seawall is hastily reinforced, cries of despair can be heard from within the city proper. The Huguenots know their days are numbered.”

The reckoning

Narrator — “@ArcticFox, your rolls are Death 14, Mention 11, Promotion 9, Crowns 9”

🎲 Jean Renault rolls 2d6 — 7 (Promotion target 9: no promotion)

Jean Renault — “For $$$”

🎲 Jean Renault rolls 2d6 — 7 (Crowns target 9: no loot)

Narrator — “An uneventful outcome.”

Jean Renault — “Survival is never uneventful!”

Jules Lavelle — Baron, Lieutenant Colonel, Royal Foot Guards

His battalion scattered into the sea, Lavelle faced the dice with no chance of plunder:

Narrator — “@Jules Lavelle, your rolls are Death 12, Mention 8, Promotion 7. No chance for crowns.”

🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 2d6 death — 5 (Death target 12: survives) 🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 2d6 mention — 3 (Mention target 8: no mention) 🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 2d6 promotion — 5 (Promotion target 7: no promotion)

Narrator — “An uneventful outcome for the scion of Lavelle.”

Slade Imbee — Subaltern, F Company, King’s Musketeers

Narrator — “Crowns received!”

Narrator — “Roll 2d6”

🎲 Slade Imbee rolls 2d6 crowns — 4

The award came with the season’s most singular honor, narrated from the GM’s own hand:

Narrator — “After the battle, as you are nursing a musket wound, the Cardinal notices you. He shakes your hand, his eyes steely, and continues down the line of injured mine. As you are gathering up your awe, his attendant drops a purse of 400 crowns into your hand. ‘Remember his Eminence’s generosity, and our great victory,’ he hisses, and follows after his master.”

Slade Imbee — “Slade is honored and dumbfounded. ‘feared the worst.’ He thinks. ‘Our near shameful marksmanship failed to deprive the English of their commanders as planned. Though we were victorious, it was not the rout that was planned for this day. I thought we would be punished. The Lord surely smiles on us and graces the Cardinal and his Eminence with generosity indeed!’.*

Smiling ear-to-ear he turns to move on to his next duty with exuberance when a twinge in his thigh halts him. ‘Oh right… perhaps a medic for first to bandage this up’”

Honors and casualties

No player character died on the seawall, and none was mentioned or promoted; the season’s whole ledger was Slade Imbee’s 400 crowns and a handshake from Cardinal Richelieu. The NPC butcher’s bill took longer to tally. In the Crown Prince Cuirassiers’ regimental channel, minutes after his own rolls:

Jean Renault — “So did any colonels die?”

Narrator (from the GM’s player account) — “Haven’t resolved the NPCs yet”

Four days later, out of character: Narrator — “Regiment rosters have been updated with deceased NPCs.”

One more small casualty of the summer, in the off-season channel while the guns still sounded — Côme Touchard’s bid for a marine’s coat:

Narrator — “@etirflita, roll to join the Royal Marines. You need a 5.”

🎲 Côme Touchard rolls 1d6 — 1 (rejected; the message drew a lone 🚫)

Table talk

Fall 1628 — The Fall of La Rochelle, and a Vortex of Leafy Death

September – November 1628 · resolved at the table 28–29 March 2022 (deployment fixed 9 February) · Mission: Field Operations · Theater: refugee checkpoints on the roads out of La Rochelle

The situation

La Rochelle was already lost when the fall season opened. After the summer’s failed English relief at the seawall, the great siege reached its end — and the army’s last task was not a battle at all, but a manhunt.

Narrator — “The Fall Campaign”

🎲 The Narrator rolls 1d6 — 6

Narrator — “This is a Field Operations campaign.”

Narrator — “The siege has cracked the city wide open. The last Huguenot holdouts and English stragglers flee La Rochelle in droves. Among their number, dozens of English commanders and French nobles, chiefly to blame for funding the multi-year rebellion, try to slip out amidst the filthy peasantry. The army, such as it is in the Fall, has been assigned inspection duty in the field, searching the endless lines of refugees for persons of interest.”

The deployment had been settled weeks earlier, in the off-season channel, when the Narrator called for volunteering rolls:

Narrator — “The following players should roll 1d6 to see if their commanders are volunteering them for the Fall Campaign: @Slade Imbee @ArcticFox @CitrusNotes”

🎲 Armand Dufour rolls 1d6 — 6 (his commander volunteers the regiment)

Narrator — “The Picardy Musketeers, including @CitrusNotes, @WillWorker, and @etirflita, will be deploying this season (unless anyone wishes to use Influence on the commander – a mere Major!)”

Armand Dufour — “To glory!”

Jean Renault’s Cuirassiers rolled a 5 and stayed home. Slade Imbee rolled a 2, then tried diplomacy:

Slade Imbee — “Am I to understand from my roll that my commanders were so… impressed with my performance in this last venture that they see my presence in the next of the utmost importance and I am to report to duty immediatly?”

Narrator — “Your commander volunteers on a 6 – you’ll be in Paris this season, unless/until you choose to volunteer on your own.”

The order of battle

Narrator — “Deploying:

Bg. Gen. @Curtis Sinnoch leading the 1st Brigade, including in the Picardy Musketeers Captains @CitrusNotes and @WillWorker, and Pvt. @etirflita.

Lt. Col. @Jules Lavelle commanding the Royal Foot Guards.

@sirsfurther has volunteered as a private in the Frontier Regiment.”

Narrator — “The Frontier Regiment is commanded by Col. Thomas Alard, a savvy veteran of the Spanish Campaigns.”

The player characters at the checkpoints:

Character Rank / Post Station
Curtis Sinnoch Brigadier-General Commanding the 1st Brigade — senior officer on the field
Armand Dufour Captain, E Company Picardy Musketeers, 1st Brigade
Albert Blastagarde Captain, F Company (“The F is for Firepower”) Picardy Musketeers, 1st Brigade
Côme Touchard Private, E Company Picardy Musketeers, 1st Brigade
Jules Lavelle Baron, Lieutenant Colonel Commanding the Royal Foot Guards
Joseph Bousain Private (volunteer) Frontier Regiment, under Col. Thomas Alard

The NPC command: Col. Thomas Alard of the Frontier Regiment, “a savvy veteran of the Spanish Campaigns,” and Maj. Jean Ouvrard, commanding the Picardy Musketeers — a man about to earn his place in the annals of produce-related warfare.

The record

Narrator — “@Curtis Sinnoch, as senior officer on the field, you may set the tone of the endeavor.”

Curtis Sinnoch — “Curtis paced the halls of Bothwells - his need to stay in Paris during the Summer campaign now unleashing months of pent up rage and frustration upon the poor, unsuspecting English. An orderly meekly started to suggest holding some strength back and was silenced with a chopping motion Composing himself, Curtis heads to the 1st battalion HQ and sends his men to gather any and all available soldiers and officers, dragging some unwilling from their beds as needed ‘We are the finest of France! We will not allow the English to sully our lands any further! At dawn, the entire 1st brigade will mobilize and quash this uprising for good! I believe the term is “overwhelming firepower” yes? What others may otherwise seem as a troublesome bother, I see as an insidious attempt to poison France herself from within! No quarter will be given, and none shall be expected! Brave sons of France - you’ve been called, to deliver upon our enemy a DIVINE RETRIBUTION! With each musket shot, LET THUNDER BELLOW! With each sabre thrust, LET LIGHTNING STRIKE! We SHALL NOT, WILL NOT allow these filth to continue to contaminate our grounds! We ride! WE RIDE TO GLORY!’”

The speech drew a 😈. In the OOC channel, two minutes after the campaign was announced, Côme Touchard’s player had already set a different tone:

etirflita (OOC) — “Leeeeeeeroyyyyyy Jeeeeenkiiiiiins!”

The 1st Brigade — Bg. Gen. Curtis Sinnoch

Narrator — “One week later, the 1st Brigade stands in bored ranks, blithely processing one refugee after another. @Curtis Sinnoch, give any relevant orders to your colonels and roll for your result.”

Curtis Sinnoch — “Men, the enemy is insidious. They will play the part of the lowly peasant until you turn your backs, then your throat is CUT! Keep your men diligent and observant! Frequent guard changes to keep our processors sharp, with lookouts both forward and aft of the stations to alert of potential issues. I want a second task force of troops behind the primary processing stations at the ready should they need to support, or better yet flank an opposing force. We know the Narrator is a Jackass, and you have full permission to hunt down his kin. You’ve all trained and studied well, and all have full permission to deviate from orders to hunt targets of opportunity - the higher the rank, the more leniency will be granted. For FRANCE!”

🎲 Bg. Gen. Sinnoch’s command roll: 1d6 — 1 (the dice bot’s message earned a lone 😴)

Narrator — “Your colonels listen closely, taking your words at face value, and the screams of peasants who’ve lost their homes and livelihoods can be heard from your checkpoints for days. In spite of it all, other than a few coins of English currency and a single English soldier in a dress doing his best French accent, your troops fail to do much more than terrorize their own countrymen. Result is a 4 - Inconclusive.”

The Picardy Musketeers — Maj. Jean Ouvrard, and the cabbage cart

Narrator — “Maj. Jean Ouvrard, commanding the Picardy Musketeers, decides to personally intervene when he notices a greengrocer’s cartful of cabbages seems oddly lumpy. He orders his men to perform a closer inspection.”

🎲 Maj. Ouvrard’s command roll: 1d6 — 1

Narrator — “A gang of wanted criminals bursts of out of the cabbages, swinging wickedly curved blades in a vortex of leafy death. The nearest musketeers are cut down instantly, and the ruffians slip away into the sea of displaced peasants. The result is 5 - Own driven from field.”

The Royal Foot Guards — Lt. Col. Jules Lavelle

Narrator — “@Jules Lavelle, give your orders and roll.”

Jules Lavelle — “Would that I were serving under my former commander! But now is Lavelle’s time to shine. Men, form orderly ranks, just like the royal promenade. We shall keep these stinking commoners moving along before our noses have a chance to take in their malodorous stench. They’re rats and rabble, spare them not a second glance!”

🎲 Lt. Col. Lavelle’s command roll: 1d6 — 2

The outcome narrations for the rest of the night were posted from the GM’s player account, but the voice is the Narrator’s:

Narrator — “As the days pass, more and more of the Royal Foot Guards turn up missing. Closer inspection reveals their bodies stashed under a nearby hedgerow. Some English spies have been cutting their throats at night watch, after the second wine ration had been given. After taking heavy losses in this way, the Guards are forced to retreat. The result is 5 - Own driven from field.”

The Frontier Regiment — Col. Thomas Alard

Narrator — “Col. Alard of the Frontier Regiment takes a more pointed approach. He orders his men to search every passing citizen, no matter the delay. The men of the Frontier Regiment are not above getting their hands dirty.”

🎲 Col. Alard’s command roll: 1d6 — 1

Narrator — “Open violence breaks out between the peasants and Frontiersmen, as the refugees accuse the soldiers of being thieves and pickpockets themselves. Some of the soldiers fire into the crowd, and the resulting battle leaves dozens of volunteers bloody or dead. Col. Alard faces court-martial for his laxity. The result is 5 - Own driven from field.”

Thus ended the field operations of Fall 1628: one Inconclusive, three Own driven from field — every defeat inflicted by cabbages, wine rations, and the French people themselves. Not one English commander was caught on the record.

And on that lowest of loot rolls, the Narrator delivered the season’s longest personal vignette — the hollow-tree judgment:

Narrator — “A fat French merchant is brought before Curtis, accused by his maid of having been a Huguenot collaborator. He listens carefully to the old woman’s story as the man sweats in the dark of the field tent. Having heard enough, Curtis dismisses her and prepare to deliver the man his judgment. ‘Please, sir,’ he begs, ‘I have great riches hidden in the hills. Wealth beyond your dreams! I will pay you, just let me go!’

The man falls to his knees, and Curtis nods slightly. ‘Give me your treasures, and I will show you mercy.’

The merchant, walking ahead, leads Curtis and his retinue out into the night. After ten minutes’ walk, they come upon a small spring surrounding by a little copse of trees. The merchant runs his hands over one of the trees, then gasps in delight, yanking the side of the tree open. Immediately, hundreds of gold coins spill out from the hollowed trunk, glittering in the torchlight.

The merchant smiles broadly. ‘There you are, sir. I give all this to you. Only let me live.’

Curtis frowns from atop his horse. ‘There is a problem here, scoundrel. This is traitor’s money; it belongs to the crown. It is not yours to give.’

The merchant still has a confused expression on his face as Curtis gives the order, and his adjutant slits the sympathizer’s throat.

As a reward for the vast riches he’s recovered, Curtis receives a permanent promotion, and a 50 crown bonus.”

Jules Lavelle — Baron, Lieutenant Colonel, Royal Foot Guards

🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 2d6 death — 4 (Death target 12: survives) 🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 2d6 mention — 3 (Mention target 10: no mention) 🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 2d6 promotion — 4 (Promotion target 7: no promotion) 🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 2d6 crowns — 8 (Crowns target 8: loot!) 🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 1d6 — 3

Narrator — “150 crowns”

Jules Lavelle — “The scion of Lavelle survives another day!”

Albert Blastagarde — Captain, F Company, Picardy Musketeers

Albert Blastagarde — “Capt. Blastagarde takes his General’s orders to heart. After all, for the past three months he has had nothing else to do but privately secure prototypes of various armaments from his family’s business for his Company… along with an ample supply of regular munitions, including a personal cannon for any soldier who requested one.

And so, as the refugees lined up for inspection, those who found themselves in the line for Company F were questioned not at sword point or with the barrel of a musket pointed at their head, but in front of a wall of cannons backed by musketeers which ensured any English invader who tried to flee would find themselves quickly and overwhelmingly surrounded by an insurmountable quantity of gun power propelled munitions ranging from pistol pellets to cannon balls. A couple of his soldiers even opted for an experimental miniature ballista which fired from a series of five auto-loaded javelins in under three seconds. And so, but for a few volleys triggered by either English scum; the overly excited; or, simply the purely terrified, the line for Company F proceeded in a largely orderly manner…”

🎲 Albert Blastagarde rolls 2d6 death — 7 (Death target 8: survives) 🎲 Albert Blastagarde rolls 2d6 mention — 7 (Mention target 10: no mention) 🎲 Albert Blastagarde rolls 2d6 promotion — 5 (Promotion target 7: no promotion) 🎲 Albert Blastagarde rolls 2d6 crowns — 8 (Crowns target 11: no crowns)

Albert Blastagarde — “Despite the lack of personal advancement, Capt. Blastagarde finds peace in the ample number of notes and feedback received from the endeavor, including initial designs for a new form of cannon ball which will mitigate against it ricocheting back at the shooter when it hits another similarly targeted cannon ball in mid flight.”

Côme Touchard — Private, E Company, Picardy Musketeers

Touchard, living “on borrowed time” since he’d refused to buy a commission back in June, declared for poltroonery — shifting his Death target from 7 up to a safer 10:

Côme Touchard — “With cowardice of +3 (and a modified death roll of 10) I flee for my life!”

🎲 Côme Touchard rolls 2d6 — 10 (Death target 7, cowardice +3 → target 10: rolls it exactly — DEAD)

Côme Touchard (at the table) — “Whoops”

Hours later, the Narrator returned to write him out in full:

Narrator — “Having hidden behind a rock and successfully avoided the wild ambush, Côme wanders over to observe the cleanup efforts and see if he can pick up any leftovers from the tontine.

Meanwhile, the greengrocer stares in horror at what’s left of his bloody, dismembered produce. Côme, noticing the man’s distress, approaches to offer a consoling word. The greengrocer turns on him, livid, and hisses ‘MY CABBAGESSSSSSS!’ before baring his teeth and going straight for Côme’s throat.

Côme fights him off, but not without losing a few bits of skin in the process. He applies a dirty bandage and thinks nothing more of the matter.

The wounds swiftly turn gangrenous, and he expires in a hospital tent a few days later.”

So died Côme Touchard — survivor of the ambush, victim of the bite — the only man in the campaign killed by the man whose cabbages the army had already destroyed. His stone joined the cemetery that same morning:

Joseph Bousain — Private (volunteer), Frontier Regiment

🎲 Joseph Bousain rolls 2d6 — 2 (Death target 6: survives) 🎲 Joseph Bousain rolls 2d6 — 7 (Mention target 10: no mention) 🎲 Joseph Bousain rolls 2d6 — 2 (Promotion target 7: no promotion) 🎲 Joseph Bousain rolls 2d6 — 9 (Crowns target 11: no crowns)

Narrator — “Congratulations on your survival.”

Honors and casualties

The Picardy Musketeers’ officer corps had fared far worse than the players:

Narrator — “Due to the deaths of nearly the entire command staff of the Picardy Musketeers, @CitrusNotes and @WillWorker have been given acting command of 1st and 3rd Battalion, respectively.” (the announcement drew a 👏)

And then the Cardinal closed the theater:

Narrator — “The campaign wraps up, and each officer receives a personal note of thanks from the Cardinal for his part in the siege and ending the Protestant menace. ‘Never again will the shores of France be sullied by the presence of those who do not worship Christ in accordance with the doctrine of the Pope in Rome,’ reads the rose-scented missive. The European theater of this bloody, all-consuming war is at an end.”

The season’s ledger: Curtis Sinnoch confirmed as permanent Brigadier-General with a 50-crown bonus (and a hollow tree’s worth of traitor’s gold recovered for the crown); Armand Dufour up 250 crowns and an acting battalion command; Albert Blastagarde an acting battalion command and some ballistics notes; Jules Lavelle 150 crowns; Joseph Bousain his life; Côme Touchard a grave. Within days the Narrator opened the spring volunteering rolls — the Picardy Musketeers and the Crown Prince Cuirassiers both declined. The armies of France were going home.

Table talk

etirflita (in general-ooc, two minutes after the campaign was announced) — “Leeeeeeeroyyyyyy Jeeeeenkiiiiiins!”

Curtis Sinnoch (mid-speech, in his official checkpoint orders) — “We know the Narrator is a Jackass, and you have full permission to hunt down his kin.”

Curtis Sinnoch (opening his resolution) — “Straight Rolls across the board! For Life!” …and, on hitting his crowns target: “Dolla Dolla Bills Y’all!”

CitrusNotes (in general-ooc, minutes after his rolls) — “Well! I survived and some coin in the pocket. Can’t complain all things considered”

Slade Imbee (on learning he had not been voluntold) — “Am I to understand from my roll that my commanders were so… impressed with my performance in this last venture that they see my presence in the next of the utmost importance and I am to report to duty immediatly?”

❦

Winter 1629 — The Ambush on the Creuse (the Last Campaign)

February – March 1629 · resolved at the table 5 – 10 June 2022 · Mission: Assault · Theater: the royal highway along the river Creuse

The situation

The seed of the season was planted a month early, on 13 May, when the orders call went out — and with it a very large box.

Narrator — “@everyone orders due for February. If you want to volunteer for the Winter Campaign, now is the time.”

Albert Blastagarde — “Having received his orders, Albert kisses his new beau farewell as his carriage is loaded with new prototypes. The final large box which required four men to lift it bears the simple marking, ‘Le Vaporisateur’”

On 5 June 2022 the announcements channel posted “February 1629,” and the campaign channel opened its final file:

Narrator — “The Winter Campaign”

Narrator — “The Minister of War is especially pleased to learn that @everyone has volunteered!”

Narrator — “Henri, Duke of Rohan, a fiendish Huguenot leader, has learned nothing from the fall of La Rochelle and the terrible suffering the Protestants brought down upon themselves there. Seeing the folly of resisting Royal forces at sea, he’s refocused his efforts inland, marching several armies overland at great speed to reach Huguenot strongholds in the South of France. One royal highway, running alongside the river Creuse, has been identified as the most likely avenue of escape for Rohan’s remaining forces.

The Frontier Regiment and volunteers have been deployed to intercept, and hopefully destroy, the Huguenots before they can return to their bases of support in the South.”

🎲 Narrator rolls 1d6 — 3

Narrator — “This is an Assault campaign.”

The order of battle

Narrator — “Bg. Gen. @Curtis Sinnoch commands the 1st Brigade of Foot, including Cpts. @CitrusNotes and @WillWorker with the Picardy Musketeers, led by Maj. Ghislain Maitron.

Lt. Col. @Jules Lavelle leads the Royal Foot Guards.

The Frontier Regiment, led by Col. Lucien Lièvremont, a seasoned and celebrated officer, has awarded temporary commissions to Lt. Col. @ArcticFox and his Crown Prince Cuirassiers 1st Squadron, as well as Cpt. @DancingHorse. Sub. @Slade Imbee and Pvt. @sirsfurther fill the ranks.”

In character terms: Brigadier General Curtis Sinnoch in overall command of the 1st Brigade of Foot; Captains Armand Dufour and Albert Blastagarde in acting command of the Picardy Musketeers’ 1st and 3rd Battalions (the entire command staff having died at La Rochelle); Lieutenant Colonel Jules Lavelle with the Royal Foot Guards; Lieutenant Colonel Jean Renault’s cuirassier squadron, Captain Abelard Soucy, Subaltern Slade Imbee, and Private Joseph Bousain all attached to Colonel Lièvremont’s Frontier Regiment. Every player character in the game marched.

The record

Narrator — “Reconnoitering cavalry report the Huguenots en route as expected. Bg. Gen. Sinnoch and Col. Maitron meet the evening before the armies will make contact to draw up the plan of battle. Over multiple servings of wine, Col. Maitron suggests a pincer movement, with his diverse forces on the right, and the 1st Brigade on the left. He imagines it will drive the enemy into the river.”

Narrator — “@Curtis Sinnoch, please give your orders and roll.”

Curtis Sinnoch — “Col. Maitron, I agree our best bet is to force the craven Huguenots towards the river is one of our best bets. However, I wish to make sure we utilize our best assets to ensure we inflict as much pain and suffering upon our foes as possible. To that end, I wish to use our Cavalry along the road to harass our foes long before the actual battle commences, hitting and running, drawing our their lines while the Frontier Regiment sabotages supply lines.

We will launch our final attack here, where the river is shallow to the side closest to highway, but plunges unexpectedly towards the far bank. We will line up the Royal Foot Guard just inside the treeline, poised to rip the enemy apart as they flounder in deeper waters. What say you?”

Curtis Sinnoch — “@Jules Lavelle you have final discretion on how to deploy your troops along the water line, but I would recommend keeping a small contingent of sharp shooters available to engage in specialty targets as they introduce themselves. Have them focus on the opposing bank to fire on incoming threats to allow the rank and file time to engage the masses. Godspeed.”

🎲 Curtis Sinnoch rolls 1d6 — 3

Narrator — “Bg. Gen. Sinnoch’s plan takes the disorganized enemy almost completely unawares. Already exhausted from a long march after a terrible defeat, and with nighttime raids and from Royal cavalry, and the resulting hunger, keeping everyone on edge, morale among the Protestant troops is at rock-bottom even before the bulk of the Royal forces present themselves.

Only a few battalions, personally commanded by Rohan himself, manage to organize themselves quickly enough to provide any sort of resistance. The river runs red with the blood of their comrades as the battle wears on. The result is 2 - Bloody victory.”

Then, unit by unit, the plan met the enemy. First the Picardy Musketeers:

Narrator — “Col. Maitron, seeking sensible glory for his Musketeers, holds them back from the battle until victory is assured. As the enemy begins to break, he finally orders the charge.”

🎲 Narrator rolls 1d6 — 1

Narrator — “His delayed charge is timed almost perfectly with the Royal Foot Guard’s major volley. Perfectly arrayed in defilade as per standard tactics, the RFG have aimed high to decapitate any mounted officers. There is a special prize out for any round that takes Rohan himself in the head.

The RFG’s best marksman, spotting the dour Duke towards the rear, takes careful aim, lights his musket, and pulls the trigger. At just that moment, the Picardy Musketeers leap onto the hill, taking dozens of balls that had been intended for the enemy in their own backs instead. The Musketeer assault collapses, and the RFG rush to help their fallen allies.

The result is 5 - Repulsed.”

Jules Lavelle — “A shambles! Bg. Gen. Sinnoch’s perfect plan – ruined! Forget this nonsense, men! Leave those Musketeer fools to their fates and follow me, for the GLORY of FRANCE! CHAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAARGE!”

🎲 Jules Lavelle rolls 1d6 — 1 (the table reacts with a plank)

Narrator — “Jules Lavelle charges forward on his horse, not taking the time to look back. His men, who had settled in for a comfortable, long-range engagement, are taking their time preparing for a charge. This is time Lavelle himself has not taken. Realizing his mistake, he turns his horse to rush back to his own lines, bellowing at his men to get to their foot.

Lavelle’s horse trips over the corpse of a slain Musketeer, and they both go down in a surprised tumble. Worried for their commander, the mass of Guardsmen toss aside their arms and rush out to help – just in time for the Duke of Rohan’s small cavalry contingent to rush in from the side, sowing chaos and bloody slaughter among the confused Guardsmen.

Lavelle can do nothing but watch as the flower of French chivalry, entrusted to his care, is cut down before his very eyes. The result is 5 - Repulsed.”

Narrator — “Col. Lièvremont plays it by-the-book as usual, securing ground and enforcing his flanks before advancing. The Frontier Regiment encircles the foe and steadily pushes him back into the river, where the Protestants, feeling their boots getting wet, panic.”

🎲 Narrator rolls 1d6 — 1 (another plank)

Narrator — “But there is only one thing more dangerous than a loose wolf, and that is a cornered wolf. With certain death at their backs, the enemy fight like demons, and the Frontier Regiment lacks the cohesion to present any kind of solid resistance to an actual counter-assault. The volunteers and penal battalions begin dropping like flies, and the military reality of plans and contact with the enemy rears its ugly head once more. The plan hasn’t survived, and neither will most of the Royal forces, as the Protestants cut a bloody swathe to freedom.

The result is 5 - Repulsed.”

As acting battalion commanders, Dufour and Blastagarde were each invited to give orders and obtain a personal battle result. Blastagarde’s order was the one the whole war had been building toward:

Albert Blastagarde — “While Albert’s men may have been cut down by miscoordinated friendly fire, at the very least they completed their assigned task and positioned ‘Le Vaporisateur’ with an unobstructed view of the enemy.

The monstrosity of six full barreled cannons held together by an aiming mechanism was intimidating on its own. But its true horror lay in its black powdered filled cannon balls designed to explode on impact… in theory.

Requiring four men to operate and one brave soul to be standing next to it when it fired, Albert was not about to let anyone else take the glory.

Albert orders the targeting of the most likely location of the Duke and, when ready, takes position beside his opus to fire it personally.”

🎲 Albert Blastagarde rolls 1d6 — 4

Narrator — “The grotesque apparatus lets out a terrible scream of overstressed iron. Two of the balls explode in their barrels, but by some miracle of metallurgy, the tubes mostly contain the force, merely splitting apart at the ends. Three of the other four balls sail out into the mass of forces, missing Rohan and his small force, but impacting amidst the densest concentration of Protestant soldiery.

The effect is immediate and horrifying. Weapons, limbs, and surprised faces, some still attached to their heads, fly in every direction. Men who haven’t bathed in weeks suddenly find themselves showered in a black liquid of mixed composition: one part river water, one part mud, and the rest the innards of their fellows.

The final ball goes high, soaring across the river entirely, to where the Royal cavalry are patiently waiting to cut down any survivors fleeing across the river. The ball fails to explode, but instead bounces along the ground, where it finds ample choice of horse legs to snap like brittle twigs in its passing. The screams of maimed horses fill the air wherever the screams of men go quiet.

The result is 3 - Pyrrhic victory.”

Dufour, grazed, trampled, and concussed, chose this moment for initiative:

Armand Dufour — “Having been merely grazed in the back by stray bullets and only lightly trampled by confused horsemen, the VERY brief loss of consciousness caused by the shockwave of the experimental seige weapon was the final sign Armand needed. Clearly luck was on his side.

With this irrefutable message from on high, and not at all a concussion-induced fantasy, Armand quietly gathers the few remaining able-bodied members of his Battalion and steals through the underbrush to form a surprise attack at the rear of the foe. ‘No one will expect us coming if we just slip in between them and the river!’ He thinks, through a painful mental fog. ‘Besides, I am dreadfully thirsty and could really use a rinse to investigate the blood stains on this uniform. Surely, they can’t ALL be from me…’”

🎲 Armand Dufour rolls 1d6 — 4

Narrator — “Despite the dangers and the battle frenzy of the pinned Protestants, there is simply no effective means of fighting on two flanks. As Rohan’s troops are whittled down, the Musketeers begin suffering more harm from friendly bayonets than Protestant blades. The fighting is fierce, but over mercilessly quickly, even though only a few of the Royal forces are left standing.

The result is 3 - Pyrrhic victory.”

The last battle result of the war belonged to Jean Renault’s cuirassiers, resolved two days later at the table (the Narrator by now posting from his player account — the voice is unmistakably the GM’s):

Jean Renault — “We will prepare an ambush down the highway, and see if we cannot route the advance!”

🎲 Jean Renault rolls 1d6 — 6

Narrator — “Wisely ignoring the orders from the Frontier Regiment, Jean leads his cavalry down the road, where they engage a separate portion of the enemy force, peeling away a major section of reinforcements that might have turned the tide. Their sacrifice to distract the bulk of Rohan’s might is heroic, but still a sacrifice – no amount of maneuver or skilled riding can overcome the sheer numbers on the side of the Protestants, who nevertheless break when Rohan himself rushes back to order a withdrawal.”

Narrator — “The result is 3 - Pyrrhic victory”

Narrator — “@ArcticFox, gain 1 MA for out-commanding your superior”

Rohan escaped south. The battle was, on paper, a French victory; the field said otherwise.

The reckoning

Albert Blastagarde — Captain, Picardy Musketeers (acting commander, 3rd Battalion)

Narrator — “@WillWorker, your rolls are Death 8, Mention 6, Promotion 7, Crowns 5.”

🎲 Albert Blastagarde rolls 2d6 — 10 (Death target 8: dies)

WillWorker — “Worth”

Narrator — “The iron horror has done its work, and can now rest. But there is no rest for the makeshift scaffolding constructed to support it and assist its aim. Certain compromises had to be made to accommodate something so unwieldy that could also be readily turned, raised, and lowered.

Recognizing the unsteadiness of the prototype’s base, Blastagarde had ordered it reinforced with long planks assembled into trusses on either side. His engineering accounted for the stress of firing, and they handled the force without any trouble. Just one of these planks was torn away by a splitting barrel. Just one was enough.

As Blastagarde surveys the carnage wrought by his creation, it teeters. His men’s shouts of terror aren’t enough to distract him from reveling in his success. His mind fills with visions of the transformation of warfare, of artillery becoming so powerful men can’t move from trenches without being, as he puts it, vaporized.

The harbinger of the future slowly, implacably, inevitably descends on its inventor, who is, far from vaporized, flattened by his inability to get out of the way of progress.”

Three planks reacted to that one. A tombstone went up in the cemetery within the hour.

Curtis Sinnoch — Brigadier General, 1st Brigade of Foot

Narrator — “@Curtis Sinnoch, your rolls are Death 12, Mention 7, Promotion 6, Crowns 0 (Automatic success)”

Curtis Sinnoch — “Curtis surveils the carnage unfolding from a makeshift scaffolding hidden in the trees near his former RFG. He curses at the folly of Maitron, and curses his own misfortune that he will have to spend time writing letters to families of lost officers. He’ll order several bottles of fine Chablis, for gifts of condolence, and for himself. He continues to survey the area, sending messages via runners to better adjust firing positions and reposition troops as needed. He even fires a pot shot or two as the opportunity allows, aiming to sow calculated discord where possible. This is not his battle to obtain glory, but to support his soldiers and ensure the filthy Protestants are scoured from the land”

Curtis Sinnoch — “No roll modifications - rolling flat”

🎲 “For life!” — Curtis Sinnoch rolls 2d6 — 10 (Death target 12: survives) 🎲 “For mention!” — Curtis Sinnoch rolls 2d6 — 7 (Mention target 7: mentioned) 🎲 “For promotion!” — Curtis Sinnoch rolls 2d6 — 8 (Promotion target 6: promoted)

Narrator — “Mentioned & Promoted!”

🎲 Curtis Sinnoch rolls 1d6 for mention amount — 6

Narrator — “+6 SP for three months, +1 for life thereafter”

Narrator — “You have received the rank of Brevet Lieutenant General.”

🎲 Curtis Sinnoch rolls 6d6 for loot — 21

Narrator — “For your initiative and genius in trimming the ranks of the Frontier Regiment in the course of victory, the Crown awards you a commander’s bonus of 2100 crowns.”

Narrator — “In addition, for your cunning and valor in command of a Brigade, you are being considered for a title. Based on your SL, you need a 4 – please adjust down if you have failed a title check since your last creation.”

Curtis Sinnoch — “Huzzah! Got it!”

Narrator — “@Curtis Sinnoch congratulations – you have been created an Earl.”

Joseph Bousain — Private, 13th Fusiliers, D Company

Narrator — “@sirsfurther, your rolls are Death 7, Mention 9, Promotion 8. No chance for crowns.”

Joseph Bousain — “Bleary eyed from a wine soaked night with some of the other D company privates, Joseph finds himself marching near the back of the company, just in front of Cpt Matthieu Hachette, a man used to commanding from the back. Although Joseph hardly possesses the greatest military mind of his age, the snatches he catches of his Cpt’s plans (Well, I’m sure the Huguenots won’t think to hide in those trees, Artillery? Never could stand the stuff myself, far too loud, I’m sure we’ll be fine with a good old fashioned infantry charge, Ah yes, but if the marsh blocks off our retreat, our men will fight all the harder!) do not fill him with confidence. From the corner of his eye, Joseph catches a glimpse of ‘Le Vaporisateur’ and is immediately entranced. The private next to him has a rather different reaction. ‘MONSTROSITY!! What an infernal machine!’ He yelps involuntarily. At this, Hachette springs up in his saddle. ‘Talking in the ranks?? What’s this!? Why aren’t you disciplining that man subaltern?’ The platoon’s subaltern, long tired of Hachette’s inconsistent disciplinary approach sighs and reaches for the private. At this, Joseph spies an opportunity, even with his short time in the company, he is familiar with Hachette’s bizarrely idiosyncratic approach to the discipline and the chain of command, and knows well his fondness for volunteers. Joseph volunteers to discipline the man himself. Hachette is pleased by this display of enthusiasm and is sure to make a note of the name Joseph gives him (Albert Demachy). Joseph grabs his victim and marches off into the forest to ‘discipline’ him, but instead leads him up to ‘Le Vaporisateur’ in the hope of being able to witness it in action. As they watch the machine collapse, Joseph decides instead to steal some of the spare ammunition which he hopes to lob into the crowds of Huguenots.”

🎲 “life” — Joseph Bousain rolls 2d6 — 6 (Death target 7: survives) 🎲 “mention” — Joseph Bousain rolls 2d6 — 6 (Mention target 9: no mention) 🎲 “promotion” — Joseph Bousain rolls 2d6 — 9 (Promotion target 8: promoted)

Narrator — “@sirsfurther, having no regiment, you are ineligible for promotion.”

Narrator — “As the battle winds down, Armand sees a rider approaching. Assuming him to be Royal reinforcements, Cpt. Dufour raises his arm in greeting. In response, the Duke of Rohan swings his saber, lopping off the offending limb as he rides off down the river.

Armand collapses to the ground, clutching at the stump while his remaining men shout impotent obscenities at the fleeing Huguenot leader. His blood mingles with the waters of the Creuse, as his spirit mingles with the great French heroes who gave their lives in defense of their home.”

Slade Imbee — Subaltern, attached to the Frontier Regiment

🎲 Slade Imbee rolls 2d6 death — 9 (Death target 8: dies) (the table reacts with a grimace) 🎲 Slade Imbee rolls 2d6 mention — 5 🎲 Slade Imbee rolls 2d6 promotion — 8

Narrator — “Slade Imbee finds himself face-to-face with an enemy officer of great distinguishment. The man wields a rapier in one hand, and the other bears a state-of-the-art hand cannon. The fuse is already lit when they engage, and the mud makes agile maneuver impossible. The officer raises the gun, and Slade senses his doom approaching.

The weapon fires, and time seems to slow down. Slade’s instincts scream to duck, but he knows he’s too late. Instead, he forces his body to twist, and by divine providence, the ball whizzes harmlessly past him, impacting in the mud some ten yards behind.

The officer fumbles to reload his weapon, a fatal error. Slade throws mud in his enemy’s face and tackles him to the ground, where he begins choking him out.

Just as the life goes out of the officer’s eyes, an explosive shell from another experimental device impacts directly on Slade’s back. He, and his victory, are never known again.”

A third stone went up in the cemetery the next morning. His promotion roll would have made the target.

Jean Renault — Lieutenant Colonel, Crown Prince Cuirassiers 1st Squadron

Narrator — “Your rolls are Death 10, Mention 5, Promotion 5, Crowns 4”

🎲 “For France!” — Jean Renault rolls 2d6 — 6 (Death target 10: survives) 🎲 “For mention in the dispatches!” — Jean Renault rolls 2d6 — 3 🎲 Jean Renault rolls 2d6 — 6 (Promotion target 5: made) 🎲 Jean Renault rolls 2d6 — 5 (Crowns target 4: made)

Narrator — “Unfortunately, there is no room for promotion in your regiment. Roll for mention instead”

Narrator — “+3SP per month for 3 months, +1 for life thereafter”

🎲 Jean Renault rolls 4d6 for loot — 17

Narrator — “The tontine your squadron had put together goes to you. You receive 1700 crowns.”

Jean Renault — “Party at the horse guards for those who survived!”

That was the last in-character line of the war, and of the game. The survivors of the Creuse: Earl Curtis Sinnoch, Brevet Lieutenant General; Colonel Jules Lavelle of the Royal Foot Guards; Lieutenant Colonel Jean Renault, seventeen hundred crowns the richer for being the last name on his squadron’s tontine; Subaltern Joseph Bousain; Captain Abelard Soucy, untouched. The dead: Captain Albert Blastagarde, crushed beneath Le Vaporisateur; Captain Armand Dufour, his arm taken by the Duke of Rohan’s own saber; Subaltern Slade Imbee, undefeated and unwitnessed. Rohan himself rode away south, and the record ends with the toast at the Horse Guards.
